      <p>
       <b>
        Hispanic America
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        Hispanoamérica
       </i>
       , or
       <i>
        América hispana
       </i>
       ), also known as
       <b>
        Spanish America
       </b>
       (Spanish:
       <i>
        América española
       </i>
       ), is the region comprising the
       <a href="/wiki/Hispanophone" title="Hispanophone">
        Spanish-speaking nations
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">
        Americas
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       These countries have significant commonalities with each other and with
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       , its former
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire#The_Empire_On_Which_The_Sun_Never_Sets:_The_Golden_Age_(1521–1643)" title="Spanish Empire">
        European metropolis
       </a>
       . In all of these countries,
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       is the main language, sometimes sharing official status with one or more
       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">
        indigenous languages
       </a>
       (such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_language" title="Guaraní language">
        Guaraní
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quechua_language" title="Quechua language">
        Quechua
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Aymara_language" title="Aymara language">
        Aymara
       </a>
       , or
       <a href="/wiki/Mayan_languages" title="Mayan languages">
        Mayan
       </a>
       ), or
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English
       </a>
       (in Puerto Rico).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">
        Catholic Christianity
       </a>
       is the predominant religion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Hispanic America is sometimes grouped together with
       <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">
        Brazil
       </a>
       under the term "
       <a href="/wiki/Ibero-America" title="Ibero-America">
        Ibero-America
       </a>
       ", meaning those countries in the Americas with cultural roots in the Iberian Peninsula.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Hispanic America also contrasts with
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">
        Latin America
       </a>
       , which includes not only Hispanic America, but also Brazil, as well as the former
       <a href="/wiki/French_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="French colonization of the Americas">
        French colonies
       </a>
       in the Western Hemisphere (areas that are now in either the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">
        Canada
       </a>
       are usually excluded).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hispanic_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           does not
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
            cite
           </a>
           any
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            sources
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hispanic_America&amp;action=edit">

           </a>

           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">
            adding citations to reliable sources
           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Colonias_europea_en_Am%C3%A9rica_siglo_XVI-XVIII.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="618" data-file-width="536" height="288" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Colonias_europea_en_Am%C3%A9rica_siglo_XVI-XVIII.png/250px-Colonias_europea_en_Am%C3%A9rica_siglo_XVI-XVIII.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Colonias_europea_en_Am%C3%A9rica_siglo_XVI-XVIII.png/375px-Colonias_europea_en_Am%C3%A9rica_siglo_XVI-XVIII.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Colonias_europea_en_Am%C3%A9rica_siglo_XVI-XVIII.png/500px-Colonias_europea_en_Am%C3%A9rica_siglo_XVI-XVIII.png 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Colonias_europea_en_Am%C3%A9rica_siglo_XVI-XVIII.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         European colonies and claimed areas in the Americas, ca. 1750.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">
        Spanish conquest of the Americas
       </a>
       began in 1492, and ultimately was part of a larger historical process of world
       <a href="/wiki/Discovery_(observation)" title="Discovery (observation)">
        discovery
       </a>
       , through which various
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        European
       </a>
       powers incorporated a considerable amount of territory and peoples in the Americas, Asia, and Africa between the 15th and 20th centuries. Hispanic America became the main part of the vast
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">
        Spanish Empire
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napoleon_I" title="Napoleon I">
        Napoleon
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">
        takeover of Spain
       </a>
       in 1808 and the consequent chaos initiated the dismemberment of the Spanish Empire, as the Hispanic American territories began their
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_American_wars_of_independence" title="Spanish American wars of independence">
        struggle for emancipation
       </a>
       . By 1830, the only remaining Spanish American and Asian territories were
       <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">
        Philippine
       </a>
       archipelago and the islands of
       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
        Cuba
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">
        Puerto Rico
       </a>
       , until the 1898
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">
        Spanish–American War
       </a>
       .
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">
        Languages
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hispanic_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Languages">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map-Romance_Latin_America.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1250" data-file-width="1000" height="275" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Map-Romance_Latin_America.svg/220px-Map-Romance_Latin_America.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Map-Romance_Latin_America.svg/330px-Map-Romance_Latin_America.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Map-Romance_Latin_America.svg/440px-Map-Romance_Latin_America.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map-Romance_Latin_America.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Linguistic map of Latin America. Spanish America in green, Portuguese America (Brazil) in orange, and French Guiana and French Caribbean in blue.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map-Most_Widely_Spoken_Native_Languages_in_Latin_America.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="390" height="231" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Map-Most_Widely_Spoken_Native_Languages_in_Latin_America.png/200px-Map-Most_Widely_Spoken_Native_Languages_in_Latin_America.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Map-Most_Widely_Spoken_Native_Languages_in_Latin_America.png/300px-Map-Most_Widely_Spoken_Native_Languages_in_Latin_America.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0c/Map-Most_Widely_Spoken_Native_Languages_in_Latin_America.png 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map-Most_Widely_Spoken_Native_Languages_in_Latin_America.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <b>
          <span style="color:blue">
           Quechua
          </span>
         </b>
         ,
         <b>
          <span style="color:#f9dc38">
           Guarani
          </span>
         </b>
         ,
         <b>
          <span style="color:#ff9922">
           Aymara
          </span>
         </b>
         ,
         <b>
          <span style="color:#cc0000">
           Nahuatl
          </span>
         </b>
         ,
         <b>
          <span style="color:#006600">
           Mayan languages
          </span>
         </b>
         ,
         <b>
          Mapudungun
         </b>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       is the official language in most Hispanic American countries, and it is spoken by the vast majority of the population.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_American_languages" title="Native American languages">
        Native American languages
       </a>
       are widely spoken in
       <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">
        Peru
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">
        Guatemala
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">
        Bolivia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">
        Paraguay
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">
        Mexico
       </a>
       , and to a lesser degree, in
       <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">
        Panama
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">
        Ecuador
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">
        Colombia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
        Venezuela
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">
        Argentina
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">
        Chile
       </a>
       amongst other countries. In some Hispanic American countries, the population of speakers of indigenous languages tend to be very small or even non-existent (e.g.
       <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">
        Uruguay
       </a>
       ). Mexico is possibly the only country that contains the largest variety of indigenous languages than any other Hispanic American country, and the most spoken native language is Nahuatl.
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">
        Peru
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quechua_languages" title="Quechua languages">
        Quechua
       </a>
       is an official language, alongside Spanish and any other indigenous language in the areas where they predominate. In
       <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">
        Ecuador
       </a>
       , while holding no official status, the closely related
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quichua" title="Quichua">
        Quichua
       </a>
       is a recognized language of the indigenous people under the country's constitution; however, it is only spoken by a few groups in the country's highlands. In
       <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">
        Bolivia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Aymara_language" title="Aymara language">
        Aymara
       </a>
       , Quechua and Guaraní hold official status alongside Spanish.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_language" title="Guaraní language">
        Guaraní
       </a>
       , along with Spanish, is an official language of
       <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">
        Paraguay
       </a>
       , and is spoken by a majority of the population (who are, for the most part, bilingual), and it is co-official with Spanish in the
       <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">
        Argentine
       </a>
       province of
       <a href="/wiki/Corrientes" title="Corrientes">
        Corrientes
       </a>
       . In
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">
        Nicaragua
       </a>
       , Spanish is the official language, but on the country's Caribbean coast English and indigenous languages such as
       <a href="/wiki/Miskito_language" title="Miskito language">
        Miskito
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sumo_language" title="Sumo language">
        Sumo
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Rama_language" title="Rama language">
        Rama
       </a>
       also hold official status.
       <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">
        Colombia
       </a>
       recognizes all indigenous languages spoken within its territory as official, though fewer than 1% of its population are native speakers of these languages.
       <a href="/wiki/Nahuatl" title="Nahuatl">
        Nahuatl
       </a>
       is one of the 62 native languages spoken by indigenous people in Mexico, which are officially recognized by the government as "national languages" along with Spanish.
      </p>
      <p>
       Other European languages spoken in Hispanic America include:
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English
       </a>
       , by some groups in
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">
        Puerto Rico
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
        German
       </a>
       , in southern
       <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">
        Chile
       </a>
       and portions of
       <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">
        Argentina
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
        Venezuela
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">
        Paraguay
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">
        Italian
       </a>
       , in Argentina, Venezuela, and Uruguay;
       <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">
        Ukrainian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">
        Polish
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">
        Russian
       </a>
       in Argentina; and
       <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">
        Welsh
       </a>
       , in southern Argentina.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yiddish_language" title="Yiddish language">
        Yiddish
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">
        Hebrew
       </a>
       can be heard around Buenos Aires. Non-European or Asian languages include
       <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">
        Japanese
       </a>
       in Peru, Bolivia, and Paraguay;
       <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">
        Korean
       </a>
       in Argentina and Paraguay;
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">
        Arabic
       </a>
       in Argentina, Colombia, Venezuela, and Chile; and
       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">
        Chinese
       </a>
       throughout South America.
      </p>
      <p>
       In several nations, especially in the Caribbean region,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Creole_languages" title="Creole languages">
        creole languages
       </a>
       are spoken. Creole languages of mainland Latin America, similarly, are derived from European languages and various African tongues.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Garifuna_language" title="Garifuna language">
        Garifuna language
       </a>
       is spoken along the Caribbean coast in
       <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">
        Honduras
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">
        Guatemala
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">
        Nicaragua
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">
        Belize
       </a>
       mostly by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garifuna_people" title="Garifuna people">
        Garifuna people
       </a>
       a mixed race
       <a href="/wiki/Zambo" title="Zambo">
        Zambo
       </a>
       people who were the result of mixing between Indigenous Caribbeans and escaped Black slaves. Primarily an
       <a href="/wiki/Arawakan_languages" title="Arawakan languages">
        Arawakan language
       </a>
       , it has influences from Caribbean and European languages.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hispanic_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">
        Cuisine
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hispanic_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Cuisine">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_cuisine" title="Hispanic cuisine">
        Hispanic cuisine
       </a>
       as the term is applied in the Western Hemisphere, is a misnomer. What is usually considered Hispanic cuisine in the United States is mostly
       <a href="/wiki/Mexican_cuisine" title="Mexican cuisine">
        Mexican
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_American" title="Central American">
        Central American
       </a>
       cuisine. Mexican cuisine is composed of mainly indigenous—
       <a href="/wiki/Aztec" title="Aztec">
        Aztec
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">
        Mayan
       </a>
       —and Spanish influences.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Mexican_cuisine" title="Mexican cuisine">
        Mexican cuisine
       </a>
       is considered
       <a href="/wiki/Intangible_cultural_heritage" title="Intangible cultural heritage">
        intangible cultural heritage
       </a>
       by UNESCO and can be found all over the United States.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the United States, with its growing Hispanic population, food staples from
       <a href="/wiki/Mexican_cuisine" title="Mexican cuisine">
        Mexican cuisine
       </a>
       and the cuisine from other Hispanic countries have become widely available. Over the years, the blending of these cuisines has produced unique American forms such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tex-Mex_cuisine" title="Tex-Mex cuisine">
        Tex-Mex cuisine
       </a>
       . This cuisine, which originated in Texas, is based on maize products, heavily spiced ground beef, cheese and tomato sauces with chilies. This cuisine is widely available not just in the United States but across other countries, where American exports are found. In Florida, Cuban food is widely available. All of these Hispanic foods in the United States have evolved in character as they have been commercially americanized by large restaurant chains and food companies.
      </p>
      <p>
       The cuisine of Spain has many regional varieties, with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediterranean" title="Mediterranean">
        Mediterranean
       </a>
       flavors based on
       <a href="/wiki/Olive_oil" title="Olive oil">
        olive oil
       </a>
       , garlic, and
       <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">
        tomatoes
       </a>
       and due to its long Atlantic and Mediterranean coastlines, has been graced with a great variety and availability of
       <a href="/wiki/Seafood" title="Seafood">
        seafood
       </a>
       . In the inland communities of Spain, there is a long tradition of cured meat of different kinds, in addition to an abundance of dishes such as roasts and stews, based on beef, pork, lamb, and poultry. The European and Arab heritage of Spain is reflected in its food, along with cosmopolitan influences beginning in the many new ingredients brought in from the New World since the 16th century, e.g. tomatoes, potatoes, or chocolate, and the more modern tastes introduced from Europe since the 19th century, especially through French and Italian dishes. It is only in the last ten years
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
          <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (January 2014)">
           when?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       that Hispanic American dishes have been introduced in Spain. In the United States and Canada, the number of Hispanic restaurants has become a growing trend, following the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Tapas" title="Tapas">
         tapas
        </a>
       </i>
       -style restaurants fashion that first appeared in North America in the 1990s.
      </p>
      <p>
       Cuban, Dominican, and Puerto Rican cuisines, on the other hand, tend to use a lot of
       <a href="/wiki/Pork" title="Pork">
        pork
       </a>
       and can depend heavily on starchy
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Root_vegetable" title="Root vegetable">
        root vegetables
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" title="Plantain (cooking)">
        plantain
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">
        rice
       </a>
       . The most prominent influences on their Spanish culinary traditions were introduced by African slaves, and to a lesser degree, French influence from Haiti and later Chinese immigrants. The use of spicy chile peppers of varying degrees of strength used as flavour enhancers in Mexican tradition is practically unknown in traditional Spanish–Caribbean dishes. The cuisine of Haiti, a country with a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francophone" title="Francophone">
        Francophone
       </a>
       majority, is very similar to its regional neighbors in terms of influences and ingredients used.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Argentine_cuisine" title="Argentine cuisine">
        Argentine
       </a>
       diet is heavily influenced by the country's position as one of the world's largest
       <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">
        beef
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">
        wine
       </a>
       producers, and by the impact that
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_ethnic_groups" title="European ethnic groups">
        European
       </a>
       immigration had on its national culture. Grilled meats are a staple of most meals as are
       <a href="/wiki/Pasta" title="Pasta">
        pastas
       </a>
       , potatoes, rice,
       <a href="/wiki/Paella" title="Paella">
        paella
       </a>
       and a variety of vegetables (Argentina is a huge exporter of agricultural products). Italian influence is also seen in the form of
       <a href="/wiki/Pizza" title="Pizza">
        pizza
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ice_cream" title="Ice cream">
        ice cream
       </a>
       , both of which are integral components of national cuisine. Chilean cuisine is similar to that of Argentina, though seafood is much more dominant in this coastal nation. As another one of the world's largest producers, wine is as much a staple drink to Chileans as beer is to Germans.
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">
        Colombia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">
        Ecuador
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">
        Peru
       </a>
       , potato dishes are typical since the potato is originally from this region. Beef and
       <a href="/wiki/Chicken" title="Chicken">
        chicken
       </a>
       are common sources of meat. In the Highlands is the
       <i>
        cuy
       </i>
       , a South American name for
       <a href="/wiki/Guinea_pig" title="Guinea pig">
        guinea pig
       </a>
       , a common meat. Given the coastal location, both countries have extensive fishing fleets, which provide a wealth of seafood options, including the signature South American dish,
       <a href="/wiki/Ceviche" title="Ceviche">
        ceviche
       </a>
       . While potato is an important ingredient in the Highlands, Rice is the main side dish on the coast.
      </p>
      <p>
       This diversity in staples and cuisine is also evident in the differing regional cuisines within the national borders of the individual countries.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Symbols">
        Symbols
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hispanic_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Symbols">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Flag">
        Flag
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hispanic_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Flag">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Hispanicity.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="424" data-file-width="757" height="112" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Flag_of_the_Hispanicity.svg/200px-Flag_of_the_Hispanicity.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Flag_of_the_Hispanicity.svg/300px-Flag_of_the_Hispanicity.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Flag_of_the_Hispanicity.svg/400px-Flag_of_the_Hispanicity.svg.png 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Hispanicity.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_Hispanic_People" title="Flag of the Hispanic People">
          Flag of Hispanic Heritage
         </a>
         . Motto:
         <i>
          Justicia, Paz, Unión y Fraternidad
         </i>
         ("Justice, Peace, Union and Fraternity").
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flag_20-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-flag-20">
           [18]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       While relatively unknown, there is a flag representing the countries of Spanish America, its people, history and shared cultural legacy.
      </p>
      <p>
       It was created in October 1933 by Ángel Camblor,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Captain_(land)" title="Captain (land)">
        captain
       </a>
       of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Uruguay" title="Military of Uruguay">
        Uruguayan army
       </a>
       . It was adopted by all the states of Spanish America during the
       <a href="/wiki/Pan-American_Conference" title="Pan-American Conference">
        Pan-American Conference
       </a>
       of the same year in
       <a href="/wiki/Montevideo" title="Montevideo">
        Montevideo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">
        Uruguay
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flag_20-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-flag-20">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The white background stands for peace, the
       <a href="/wiki/Inti" title="Inti">
        Inti
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_deity" title="Solar deity">
        sun god
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Inca_mythology" title="Inca mythology">
        Inca mythology
       </a>
       symbolizes the light shining on the Americas, and the three crosses represent
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
        Christopher Columbus
       </a>
       '
       <a href="/wiki/Caravel" title="Caravel">
        caravels
       </a>
       , the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Ni%C3%B1a" title="Niña">
         Niña
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Pinta_(ship)" title="Pinta (ship)">
         Pinta
        </a>
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_(ship)" title="Santa María (ship)">
         Santa María
        </a>
       </i>
       , used in his
       <a href="/wiki/Voyages_of_Christopher_Columbus" title="Voyages of Christopher Columbus">
        first voyage
       </a>
       from Spain to the
       <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">
        New World
       </a>
       in 1492. The
       <a href="/wiki/Lilac_(color)#Deep_lilac" title="Lilac (color)">
        deep lilac
       </a>
       color of the crosses evokes the color of the
       <a href="/wiki/Lion" title="Lion">
        lion
       </a>
       on the
       <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">
        coat of arms
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">
        medieval
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">
        Crown of Castile
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="References">

      </h2>
      <div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">
       <ol class="references">
        <li id="cite_note-1">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-1">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          All of the following dictionaries only list "Spanish America" as the name for this cultural region. None list "Hispanic America." All list the
          <a href="/wiki/Demonym" title="Demonym">
           demonym
          </a>
          for the people of the region discussed in this article as the sole definition, or one of the definitions, for "Spanish American". Some list "Hispanic," "Hispanic American" and "Hispano-American" as
          <a href="/wiki/Synonym" title="Synonym">
           synonyms
          </a>
          for "Spanish American." (All also include as a secondary definition for these last three terms,
          <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">
           persons residing in the United States of Hispanic ancestry
          </a>
          .)
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/The_American_Heritage_Dictionary_of_the_English_Language" title="The American Heritage Dictionary of the English Language">
            The American Heritage Dictionary of the English Language
           </a>
          </i>
          (3rd ed.) (1992). Boston: Houghton Mifflin.
          <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
           ISBN
          </a>
          <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-395-44895-6" title="Special:BookSources/0-395-44895-6">
           0-395-44895-6
          </a>
          .

            Merriam-Webster's Collegiate Dictionary

          </i>
          (11th ed.) (2003). Springfield: Merriam-Webster.
          <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
           ISBN
          </a>
          <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-87779-807-9" title="Special:BookSources/0-87779-807-9">
           0-87779-807-9

          <i>

         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-2">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-2">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          "Hispanic America" is used in some older works such as Charles Edward Chapman's 1933
          <i>
           Colonial Hispanic America: A History
          </i>
          and 1937
          <i>
           Republican Hispanic America: A History
          </i>
          (both New York: The Macmillan Co.); or translated titles that faithfully reproduce
          <i>
           Hispanoamérica
          </i>
          , such as Edmund Stephen Urbanski (1978),
          <i>
           Hispanic America and its Civilization: Spanish Americans and Anglo-Americans
          </i>
          , Norman: University of Oklahoma Press. The Cambridge University Press textbook by two distinguished historians of early Latin America,
          <a href="/wiki/James_Lockhart_(historian)" title="James Lockhart (historian)">
           James Lockhart
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/Stuart_B._Schwartz" title="Stuart B. Schwartz">
           Stuart B. Schwartz
          </a>
          is entitled,
          <i>
           Early Latin America: A History of Colonial Spanish America and Brazil
          </i>
          1983.
